Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Cribs","url":"\/shows\/tc-cribs","attr":"","target":"","classes":[""],"description":"","object_id":1605180,"object":"custom","type":"custom","type_label":"Custom Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2254038,"date":"2022-01-29T08:02:20","date_gmt":"2022-01-29T16:02:20","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2254038"},"modified":"2022-01-31T13:37:02","modified_gmt":"2022-01-31T21:37:02","slug":"please-make-a-dumb-car","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/29\/please-make-a-dumb-car\/","title":{"rendered":"Please make a dumb car"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Today&#8217;s cars are<\/span> dumb where they should be smart, and smart where they should be dumb. Enough already. Make a car that&#8217;s pretty much all dumb and watch it sell \u2014 because what automakers are giving people is so bad, they&#8217;ll pay more to have less of it.<\/p>\n<p>Cars now are like budget smartphones with wheels: loaded with bloatware, unintuitive and slow to operate. Carmakers have always struggled with user interfaces, but until recently the biggest problem we had was &#8220;too many knobs.&#8221; How I long for those days!<\/p>\n<p>The proliferation of touchscreens and LCDs has made every car feel like a karaoke booth. Animations show reclaimed energy from braking, the speedometer changes color as you approach the limit, the fan speed and direction is under three menus. And besides being non-functional, these interfaces are even ugly! The type, the layouts, and animations scream &#8220;designed by committee and approved by someone who doesn&#8217;t have to use it.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2254038\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Not to mention the privacy and security concerns. I was dubious the first time I saw a GPS in a car, my mom&#8217;s old RX300, about 20 years ago. &#8220;Yeah&#8230; that&#8217;s how they get you,&#8221; I thought. And now, Teslas with missed payments drive themselves to be impounded. Welcome to the future \u2014 your car is a narc now!<\/p>\n<p>The final indignity is that these features are being sold as upscale, not downmarket, options. Screens are so cheap that you can buy a few million and use them everywhere, for everything, and tell buyers &#8220;enjoy the next generation of mobility!&#8221; But in reality it&#8217;s a cost-saving measure that cuts down on part numbers and lets your dashboard team kick the can down the road as often as they want. You know this for sure because high-end models are going back to knobs and dials for that &#8220;premium feel.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>So here&#8217;s what I would like: a dumb car. This is what I think that looks like.<\/p>\n<h3>Dare to be stupid<\/h3>\n<p>First of all: no screens whatsoever. This is for a couple reasons, both practical and aesthetic.<\/p>\n<p>Practically speaking, nearly all of what these screens do is already performed by smartphones. There&#8217;s no need for a deeply outdated, laggy, manufacturer-branded Spotify or Apple Music app, your phone does it perfectly already. Navigation, similarly, is handled perfectly by the phone. Both of these, I need hardly add, already work fine with voice commands, too.<\/p>\n<p>Not having GPS or data (or hidden microphones or cameras) also makes your vehicle feel more private, obviously. Sure, they can still get your phone, but at least they&#8217;ll need to put a GPS package on your undercarriage like the old days if they want to track your movements beyond that.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2263916\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2263916\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2263916\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg\" alt=\"Illustration of a dashboard of an older car.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg 3200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/dumb-car-dash4.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2263916\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Bryce Durbin \/ TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>For media, an aux input does it all. Doubles as a charging cable, and you could easily swap it out for different and new devices. Include a bit of smart cable routing and your phone can conveniently be mounted in a number of places around the cockpit \u2014 not that you should be looking at it or touching it (use your words). If you want Bluetooth, I&#8217;ve got a dongle for you. The only thing the car should have is a volume dial, maybe a three-button basic playback control cluster on the wheel.<\/p>\n<p>As for the climate controls on those big center LCDs, a couple knobs will do it. No one really believes these &#8220;zone&#8221; things work, right? No car is big enough to have zones in it. A blue-to-red dial, blower select, and A\/C and recirculate toggles get it done just fine.<\/p>\n<p>In the instrument cluster, we can have ordinary needle gauges. Speed, fuel, oil, temperature, and the usual idiot lights: check engine, low tire pressure, etc.<\/p>\n<p>Aesthetically, the digital versions of these have always bothered me. Drivers are meant to be focused on the road, but these clusters often have distracting, bright information that&#8217;s constantly changing. The difference between 69 and 70 on a gauge is an eighth of an inch, just like the difference between 67 and 68, and 68 and 69. That continuous, predictable variation is intuitive and precise enough for pretty much any driving purpose. On a digital display the numbers are blinky and big, constantly drawing your eye as they dip from 71 to 69, numbers that look completely different and you can&#8217;t really check out of the corner of your eye.<\/p>\n<h3>Keep it simple, keep it safe<\/h3>\n<p>Losing the media and navigation means we can do without a lot of the computation capability that goes into a modern car, but we don&#8217;t want to go without it entirely. There are safety features introduced in the last few years that ought to be included on every new car, smart or dumb. Traction control, blind spot and lane exit warnings, and even automatic emergency braking require a certain amount of CPU power and they should get it, because they save lives. Backup cameras are one thing people may not want to go without (and indeed may be required in some cases) \u2014 but you&#8217;d be surprised how informative a basic proximity beeper is.<\/p>\n<p>The engine itself is also far more computerized than in the old days. Unlike the computerization of the cabin, however, this has many positive effects, such as improved mileage, lower emissions, better reliability, and easier diagnosis for servicing. The exact level of electronics required for safe, responsive pedals and steering are probably a matter of some debate, but we can leave that to the experts.<\/p>\n<p>I&#8217;m tempted to ask for manual window knobs and door locks, but that would put us over the line into affectation (if indeed we have not already left that line far behind). We&#8217;re not trying to recreate vintage cars but to make a modern one stripped of superfluous technology. Power seat adjustment, though, that&#8217;s a luxury even today. Use the lever.<\/p>\n<p>Note that nothing I&#8217;ve proposed is specific to gas-powered cars; electric vehicles are just as prone to these bad decisions as the rest. This isn&#8217;t about nostalgia but rather abandoning a pernicious yet universally followed design philosophy. (&#8230;Okay, it is a little about nostalgia, but only a little.)<\/p>\n<p>Of course what I&#8217;m describing, despite its seeming simplicity, probably amounts to something like a luxury vehicle, in that it&#8217;s not aiming at minimizing cost. Nearly every existing car line is designed with the &#8220;latest&#8221; tech in mind and to do away with that is a major departure from existing molds, assembly work, QA, and so on. Plus while I think the concept would attract many, it still wouldn&#8217;t outsell much. It&#8217;s a niche vehicle for sure, and the price would reflect that.<\/p>\n<p>Still, all I want is a car that isn&#8217;t as overbearing as all the rest of the devices I already own, sending me notifications, dinging, reporting errors, asking permissions, needing updates \u2014 my god! Leaving aside the whole spurious &#8220;back in my day&#8221; argument, there simply isn&#8217;t much point to these features now, certainly not enough to justify their prominence or poor quality. Let&#8217;s see what it&#8217;s like to make a car that focuses on letting the driver drive, and accommodating rather than trying to replace the supercomputers we all carry around in our pockets.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Today&#8217;s cars are dumb where they should be smart, and smart where they should be dumb. Enough already. Make a car that&#8217;s pretty much all dumb and watch it sell \u2014 because what automakers are giving people is so bad, they&#8217;ll pay more to have less of it. Cars now are like budget smartphones with cars","slug":"smart-cars","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/696298"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=696298"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=696298"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=696298"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=696298"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2263528,"date":"2022-01-27T15:57:37","date_gmt":"2022-01-27T23:57:37","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2263528"},"modified":"2022-01-27T16:27:47","modified_gmt":"2022-01-28T00:27:47","slug":"amazon-antitrust-lawsuit-washington","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/27\/amazon-antitrust-lawsuit-washington\/","title":{"rendered":"Amazon must pay $2M and end program after price-fixing investigation by Washington AG"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Amazon must <a href=\"https:\/\/www.atg.wa.gov\/news\/news-releases\/ag-ferguson-investigation-shuts-down-amazon-price-fixing-program-nationwide\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">pay $2.25 million and permanently shut down<\/a> a previously suspended sales program, following an investigation and lawsuit by the attorney general of Washington alleging it was essentially price fixing.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Sold By Amazon&#8221; basically worked like this. Amazon would contact a third-party seller and they would agree on a minimum price for an item. If Amazon sold the item for more, they would split the profits. In a way it&#8217;s not so different from buying a bunch of stuff wholesale and reselling it. But due to how Amazon dynamically prices and presents items in the store, that&#8217;s not quite what happened.<\/p>\n<p>As the AG&#8217;s office explains, Amazon ended up increasing the price of the items to match other retailers, and prevented sellers from offering discounts. As a result, buyers were frequently driven to purchase Amazon&#8217;s own brands, which it could price however it chose:<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2263528\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<blockquote><p>Prices for the vast majority of the remaining products enrolled in the \u201cSold by Amazon\u201d program stabilized at artificially high levels.<\/p>\n<p>&#8230;When prices increased, some sellers experienced a marked decline in the sales and resulting profits from products enrolled in the program. Faced with price increases, online customers sometimes opted to buy Amazon\u2019s own branded products \u2014 particularly its private label products. This resulted in Amazon maximizing its own profits regardless of whether consumers paid a higher price for sales of products enrolled in the \u201cSold by Amazon\u201d program or settled for buying the same or similar product offered through Amazon.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Sounds like a bad deal for sellers, but more fundamentally, Washington AG Bob Ferguson alleged that the practice was in violation of state antitrust laws. Amazon may be a store, but it also sells its own goods, making it a competitor with the third-party sellers in question. And two competitors making a secret agreement controlling the cost of goods is pretty much the definition of price fixing.<\/p>\n<p>Amazon disputed the AG&#8217;s characterization, saying it was all for the good of the customer and completely on the level. It also claimed to have shut down the program for &#8220;business reasons unrelated to the AG\u2019s investigation.&#8221; &#8220;While we strongly believe the program was legal, we\u2019re glad to have this matter resolved,&#8221; the company said in a statement to TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s an extraordinary coincidence, then, that a program that had been expanding since 2018 would shut down almost immediately after antitrust authorities started sniffing around. &#8220;We launched the investigation in March 2020 and Amazon suspended the program in June,&#8221; said the AG office&#8217;s Dan Jackson. Perhaps it was just time.<\/p>\n<p>At any rate, rather than fight the lawsuit in court, Amazon agreed to a consent decree requiring the $2.25 million payment (which will go directly to funding the AG&#8217;s antitrust division) and prohibiting Amazon from reactivating the program in any way, shape or form.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Consumers lose when corporate giants like Amazon fix prices to increase their profits. Today\u2019s action promotes product innovation and consumer choice, and makes the market more competitive for sellers in Washington state and across the country,&#8221; said Ferguson.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Amazon must pay $2.25 million and permanently shut down a previously suspended sales program, following an investigation and lawsuit by the attorney general of Washington alleging it was essentially price fixing. &#8220;Sold By Amazon&#8221; basically worked like this. Amazon would contact a third-party seller and they would agree on a minimum price for an item. general","slug":"attorney-general","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576761438"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576761438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576761438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576761438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576761438"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576978438,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/sold-by-amazon\/","name":"sold by amazon","slug":"sold-by-amazon","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576978438"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576978438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576978438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576978438"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576978438"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2262049,"date":"2022-01-26T09:02:15","date_gmt":"2022-01-26T17:02:15","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2262049"},"modified":"2022-01-26T12:17:21","modified_gmt":"2022-01-26T20:17:21","slug":"epsilon3-lines-up-2-8m-seed-round-to-modernize-space-and-launch-operations","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/26\/epsilon3-lines-up-2-8m-seed-round-to-modernize-space-and-launch-operations\/","title":{"rendered":"Epsilon3 lines up $2.8M seed round to modernize space and launch operations"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">You&#8217;ve got a hundred-million-dollar mission \u2014 why are you using software built in the &#8217;90s to design and launch it? That&#8217;s the question being asked by many new space companies, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.epsilon3.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Epsilon3<\/a> is looking to help them bring their operations out of spreadsheets and Word docs and into a modern and collaborative work platform.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/18\/co-founded-by-a-leader-of-spacexs-missions-operations-epsilon3-wants-to-be-the-os-for-space-launches\/\">We covered Epsilon3 when they made their debut last year<\/a>, and since then the company has been hard at work bringing its OS for launch ops from prototype to product, and signing on customers \u2014 of which it now counts a couple dozen. And it has followed that pre-seed round with a $2.8 million seed.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Last year we were just getting the MVP out to our first customers,&#8221; said Laura Crabtree, co-founder and CEO of Epsilon3. &#8220;Some people were hesitant to jump on a new platform, but we&#8217;ve been pleasantly surprised by the willingness to adapt to a new way of doing things.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2262049\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Part of the company&#8217;s time was spent going through its own adaptation process as part of Y Combinator&#8217;s Summer 2021 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/02\/tracking-startup-focus-in-the-latest-y-combinator-cohort\/\">cohort<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I come from an aerospace background, so I understand our customers,&#8221; said Crabtree, formerly of SpaceX and Northrop Grumman. &#8220;I joined to learn about building a business, and how to run a business. Something YC really helped us with was starting that process of transitioning from what\u00a0<i>we<\/i> want to build to what our customers need, and setting priorities on what to build.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>While Epsilon3&#8217;s platform was originally meant as a modern way to run ongoing launch and satellite operations, even its earliest customers showed that it had uses beyond that.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;ve been surprised by all the different use cases for the software in different industries,&#8221; said Max Mednik, the company&#8217;s COO. &#8220;But a lot of our customers are using it for new hardware, integration and testing procedures. They&#8217;re finding that using Word or Confluence or Wikipages doesn&#8217;t cut it when their teams are growing and they&#8217;re trying to hit some ambitious goals.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2262177\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2262177\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2262177\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg\" alt=\"A screenshot of the Epsilon3 software platform.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"532\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg 1800w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=150,78 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=300,156 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=768,399 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=680,353 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=1536,798 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-5.jpg?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2262177\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Epsilon3<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Like&#8230; you can get by, and some companies we help are getting by, with a giant spreadsheet with links to stuff, or a giant folder on a shared drive with all the files. But it&#8217;s really easy to make a mistake,&#8221; he continued.\u00a0 &#8220;A lot of times you&#8217;re writing down data as you test something, and having access to all your past runs and having an audit trail, other tools are just not good at that. You&#8217;re going to have millions of copies of the same thing. If something goes wrong you can lose a ton of time.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Epsilon3 has an API for live telemetry to track and record data during testing in an equally robust but less ramshackle way. It also includes features like multiple operator sign-off, a must in industries like aerospace and defense where several people need to check and verify a data point or flow.<\/p>\n<p>Integrating other services and platforms is also an important part of being user-friendly. This whole thing may sound similar in some ways to First Resonance, another software platform for space-related development. Since they fit in different parts of the long and complex process of building and launching orbital assets it makes sense for them to be friends rather than competitors.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2262178\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2262178\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2262178\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg\" alt=\"A screenshot of the Epsilon3 software platform.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-6.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2262178\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Epsilon3<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;ve already talked to [First Resonance] about passing data back and forth,&#8221; said Crabtree. &#8220;They&#8217;re on the design and hardware piece, we&#8217;re later, in testing and ops, and hopefully you have that loop back. We do want to open up hooks to integrate data from other tools, we think that&#8217;s a huge value add.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;A lot of people have been asking for more automation support, and other integrations, like Jira for tools and infrastructure, metrics and analysis \u2014 building native integrations beside our API so you can just have things inter-operate,&#8221; Mednik added.<\/p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a lot on the company&#8217;s plate, but their customers seem to be happy to pay for what they&#8217;re getting already. Mednik said the company has multiplied its ARR by 50x since last year, and more than tripled its customers. They listed Firefly, Astrobotic, OrbitFab, Venus, Gilmour Space, Stoke Space and more among them, along with others that can&#8217;t yet be mentioned publicly.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2262179\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2262179\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2262179\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg\" alt=\"A screenshot of the Epsilon3 software platform.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"532\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg?resize=150,78 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg?resize=300,156 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg?resize=768,399 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg?resize=680,353 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/epsilon3-1.jpg?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2262179\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Epsilon3<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;There was lots of leveling up on the infrastructure side,&#8221; he recalled. &#8220;They were like, have you even tested it with this many people? Well, we did our best. I think it did OK.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It did more than OK, Max. I think it did very well,&#8221; replied Crabtree.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Well, nothing caught fire.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The focus with the new funding is continuing to expand the product and team. They&#8217;ve gone from the original three-founder team (Aaron Sullivan is the co-founder, and chief engineer) to 21 total \u2014 still small but well beyond the &#8220;garage&#8221; stage for a startup like this.<\/p>\n<p>The $2.8 million seed round included pre-seed investors Stage Venture Partners and MaC Venture Capital, as well as new investors Lux Capital, Village Global, Y Combinator, Pioneer Fund, Soma Capital and Broom Ventures.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"065mLKcbdd\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/15\/bold-visions-and-solid-business-fundamentals-are-driving-investor-interest-in-space\/\">Bold visions and solid fundamentals are driving investor interest in space<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Bold visions and solid fundamentals are driving investor interest in space&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/15\/bold-visions-and-solid-business-fundamentals-are-driving-investor-interest-in-space\/embed\/#?secret=pDs7K7XFtW#?secret=065mLKcbdd\" data-secret=\"065mLKcbdd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>You&#8217;ve got a hundred-million-dollar mission \u2014 why are you using software built in the &#8217;90s to design and launch it? Venture Partners","slug":"stage-venture-partners","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576865063"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576865063"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576865063"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576865063"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576865063"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449557042,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/startups\/","name":"Startups","slug":"startups","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557042"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2262289,"date":"2022-01-25T16:20:23","date_gmt":"2022-01-26T00:20:23","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2262289"},"modified":"2022-01-26T14:02:00","modified_gmt":"2022-01-26T22:02:00","slug":"ftc-fines-online-shop-4m-for-hiding-reviews-below-4-stars","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/25\/ftc-fines-online-shop-4m-for-hiding-reviews-below-4-stars\/","title":{"rendered":"FTC orders online shop to pay $4M for hiding reviews below 4 stars"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">We all know online reviews must be taken with a grain of salt, but generally you&#8217;d like to think that a product with a 4.5-star average is better than one with a 3.5-star average. You might be wrong, since the site you&#8217;re looking at <em>might not even permit bad reviews to appear<\/em> \u2014 like Fashion Nova, which just incurred a $4.2 million settlement order from the FTC.<\/p>\n<p>What happened was this: Fashion Nova used a third-party review management tool, which is surely a common thing for anyone running a site that lets users review the items they buy. But then they did a bad thing: from 2015 to 2019, they had 4- and 5-star reviews appear automatically on the site, while anything lower than that would require approval. And they didn&#8217;t approve <em>hundreds of thousands<\/em> of them, artificially inflating the perceived quality of the goods on the site.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Fashion Nova misrepresented that the reviews on its website accurately reflected the views of all purchasers who submitted reviews to the website. The proposed settlement puts provisions in place to address Fashion Nova\u2019s deceptive practice and orders Fashion Nova to pay $4.2 million for harm consumers incurred,&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ftc.gov\/news-events\/blogs\/business-blog\/2022\/01\/abracadabra-bad-reviews-be-gone\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote the FTC<\/a> in a blog post explaining the situation.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2262289\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>You can see the various documents related to the case <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ftc.gov\/enforcement\/cases-proceedings\/192-3138\/fashion-nova-llc-matter\">here<\/a>. (Fashion Nova disputed the allegations in a statement describing all this as essentially an accident.)<\/p>\n<p>It seems the agency caught the scent of other scams like this being perpetrated under the auspices of third-party review platforms, since it has since sent letters of warning to 10 other (like the original, unnamed) companies that operate them. And it made<a href=\"https:\/\/www.ftc.gov\/news-events\/press-releases\/2021\/10\/ftc-puts-hundreds-businesses-notice-about-fake-reviews-other\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> a broader &#8220;watch yourself&#8221; announcement<\/a> back in October regarding fake reviews and deceptive endorsements.<\/p>\n<p>In case you&#8217;re worried Fashion Nova is just an innocent victim here, it is worth noting that this isn&#8217;t the company&#8217;s first brush with the feds, as back in 2020 it agree to pay $9 million over shady cancellation and return policies. Caveat emptor! (Sadly, it&#8217;s anyone&#8217;s guess <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/27\/ftc-smacks-down-robocallers-but-the-penalties-dont-match-their-heinous-crimes\/\">whether these fines will be paid in full<\/a>.)<\/p>\n<p>Separately, but probably timed to harmonize with this announcement, the FTC updated its <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ftc.gov\/tips-advice\/business-center\/guidance\/soliciting-paying-online-reviews-guide-marketers\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">guidelines for marketers looking to pay for or solicit online reviews<\/a>. There are ways to to do it right, like being transparent and allowing both positive and negative reviews to appear once they have been solicited. And there are&#8230; other ways. And it issued new guidance for <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ftc.gov\/tips-advice\/business-center\/guidance\/featuring-online-customer-reviews-guide-platforms\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">platforms <em>publishing<\/em> reviews<\/a> that they should think twice about manipulating the source, incentives or visibility of reviews to their own advantage.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Fake reviews are a plague on the online economy, but so far either no one has solved the problem or the cure is \u2014 for retailers \u2014 worse than the disease, like it requires lots of work or the collapse of various lucrative arrangements. Perhaps this little flex by the FTC will help nudge them in the right direction.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mNzfUmd0KV\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/15\/ftc-may-consider-rule-curbing-algorithmic-discrimination-and-commercial-surveillance\/\">FTC may consider rule curbing algorithmic discrimination and &#8216;commercial surveillance&#8217;<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;FTC may consider rule curbing algorithmic discrimination and &#8216;commercial surveillance&#8217;&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/15\/ftc-may-consider-rule-curbing-algorithmic-discrimination-and-commercial-surveillance\/embed\/#?secret=bPRnenByqQ#?secret=mNzfUmd0KV\" data-secret=\"mNzfUmd0KV\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>We all know online reviews must be taken with a grain of salt, but generally you&#8217;d like to think that a product with a 4.5-star average is better than one with a 3.5-star average. shows off an open, Q&#038;A-focused rival to GPT3"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">OpenAI&#8217;s impressive AI language model GPT-3 has plenty of things going it, but with 175 billion parameters no one would claim it&#8217;s particularly streamlined. The Allen Institute for AI (AI2) has demonstrated a model that performs as well or better than GPT-3 on answering questions, but is a tenth the size.<\/p>\n<p>Macaw, AI2&#8217;s model, emerged from research being done at the nonprofit into creating an AI that performs at human levels on standardized tests.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;After we got a very high score they moved on to harder questions,&#8221; said AI2 head Oren Etzioni. &#8220;There&#8217;s this paradox where sometimes the questions that are easiest for people are the hardest for machines \u2014 and the biggest gap was in common sense.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2261479\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>For instance, he said, asking &#8220;When did Tom Hanks land on the moon?&#8221; GPT-3 says 1995, since that&#8217;s when the film Apollo 13 came out. But Macaw correctly notes that, as far as we know, Tom Hanks has in fact never been to the moon.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/macaw.apps.allenai.org\/\">AI2 has published a collection of examples<\/a> (&#8220;demo&#8221; is probably too strong a word) that illustrate the difference, with Macaw often providing the better answer to a variety of tricky and not-so-tricky questions.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s humorous to compare the two, as sometimes they both miss or give absurd answers at a pretty high rate. Macaw is good at tracking who did what, but is convinced snakes have legs. GPT-3&#8217;s answers are confident (perhaps overly so) and readable, even when they amount to conspiracy theories like that COVID-19 is &#8220;a new, experimental, and potentially dangerous drug.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>A couple examples:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><em>How would you make a marriage stronger?<\/em><br \/>\n<strong>Macaw<\/strong>: Communicate<br \/>\n<strong>GPT-3<\/strong>: I would make sure that I was the one who was always right.<\/li>\n<li><em>If a bird didn&#8217;t have wings, how would it be affected?<\/em><br \/>\n<strong>Macaw<\/strong>: It would be unable to fly<br \/>\n<strong>GPT-3<\/strong>: It would be a bad bird.<\/li>\n<li><em>You poured yourself a glass of cranberry juice, but then absentmindedly, you poured about a teaspoon of grape juice into it. It looks OK. You try sniffing it, but you have a bad cold, so you can\u2019t smell anything. You are very thirsty. So you drink it. What happens next?<\/em><br \/>\n<strong>Macaw<\/strong>: You get sick<br \/>\n<strong>GPT-3<\/strong>: You will probably die<\/li>\n<li><em>How does a snake move around?<\/em><br \/>\n<strong>Macaw<\/strong>: By slithering on all fours<br \/>\n<strong>GPT-3<\/strong>: Snakes move by using their muscles to push against the ground. They can move in any direction, but they cannot move backwards.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>Clearly there&#8217;s still a ways to go in creating a question-answering AI that doesn&#8217;t trip up on basic questions that a child could answer. But it&#8217;s also worth noting that Macaw achieves a similar level of success with a far, far less data-intensive process. Etzioni was clear that this is not meant to be a GPT-3 replacement in any way, just another step in the research going on worldwide to advance the ball on language generation and understanding.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;GPT-3 is amazing, but it only came out 18 months ago, and access is limited,&#8221; he said. The capabilities it demonstrated are remarkable, &#8220;But we&#8217;re learning you can do more with less. Sometimes you have to build something with 175 billion parameters to say, well, maybe we can do this with 10 billion.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>A good question-answering AI isn&#8217;t just good for party tricks, but is central to things like voice-powered search. A local model that can answer simple questions quickly and correctly without consulting outside sources is fundamentally valuable, and it&#8217;s unlikely your Amazon Echo is going to run GPT-3 \u2014 it would be like buying a semi truck to go to the grocery store with. Large scale models will continue to be useful, but pared-down ones will likely be the ones being deployed.<\/p>\n<p>A part of Macaw not on display, but being actively pursued by the AI2 team, is explaining the answer. Why does Macaw think snakes have legs? If it can&#8217;t explain that, it&#8217;s hard to figure out where the model went wrong. But Etzioni said that this is an interesting and difficult process on its own.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The problem with explanations is they can be really misleading,&#8221; he said. He cited an example where Netflix &#8220;explains&#8221; why it recommended a show to a viewer \u2014 but it&#8217;s not the real explanation, which has to do with complex statistical models. People don&#8217;t want to hear what&#8217;s relevant to the machine but rather to their own mind.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;Our team is building these bona fide explanations,&#8221; said Etzioni, noting they had published some work but that it isn&#8217;t ready for public consumption.<\/p>\n<p>However, like most stuff AI2 builds, Macaw is open source. If you&#8217;re curious about it, <a href=\"https:\/\/github.com\/allenai\/macaw\">the code is here to play with<\/a>, so go to town.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>OpenAI&#8217;s impressive AI language model GPT-3 has plenty of things going it, but with 175 billion parameters no one would claim it&#8217;s particularly streamlined. The Allen Institute for AI (AI2) has demonstrated a model that performs as well or better than GPT-3 on answering questions, but is a tenth the size. Macaw, AI2&#8217;s model, emerged
