https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1182"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":45141,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/streaming\/","name":"streaming","slug":"streaming","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/45141"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=45141"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=45141"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=45141"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=45141"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2257619,"date":"2022-01-13T10:42:37","date_gmt":"2022-01-13T18:42:37","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2257619"},"modified":"2022-01-13T14:19:22","modified_gmt":"2022-01-13T22:19:22","slug":"the-m11-is-leicas-new-flagship-rangefinder","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/13\/the-m11-is-leicas-new-flagship-rangefinder\/","title":{"rendered":"The M11 is Leica&#8217;s new flagship rangefinder"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Leica&#8217;s a strange one. It only puts out a handful of cameras every year, and most of them are remixes or minor iterations on previous models. Since 2017 its flagship has been the solid but still somewhat archaic M10, but now the company has revealed its successor: <a href=\"https:\/\/leica-camera.com\/en-US\/photography\/cameras\/m\/m11-black\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the even more solid and also still somewhat archaic M11<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Leica really defined the rangefinder style in cameras, and its film models are legendary. In the digital era they are known more for their prices than anything else. While the build and image quality of the M10, Q2 and other cameras was unimpeachable, you could get a lot more camera for considerably less money elsewhere. That won&#8217;t change with the M11, but at least the new model brings some much-needed modern features.<\/p>\n<p>Perhaps the most important is the switch to a backside-illuminated sensor. This misleading term refers to putting the light-sensitive part of the sensor toward the aperture rather than letting it sit behind wiring and other components. BSI sensors usually outperform their traditional predecessors by quite a lot, and Leica generally has a good sensor game to begin with. Interestingly, they seem to have chosen a non-Bayer sub-pixel layout with an eye toward superior pixel binning.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2257619\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The new full-frame, 60-megapixel BSI sensor can be shot at full resolution, of course, but hardly anyone needs that these days. The 36MP and 18MP options sample the entire sensor rather than just lines or regions, reducing noise and artifacts. If I got one of these I&#8217;d switch it to 36MP and never look back. There are also 1.3x and 1.8x crop modes for those who enjoy them.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2257658\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2257658\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2257658\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg\" alt=\"A Leica M11 on a table plugged into a phone.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"460\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg 2500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=150,67 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=300,135 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=768,345 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=680,306 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=1536,691 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=2048,921 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Leica_M11_black_02_cable_3840x1348.jpg?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2257658\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Leica<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>There are now three easily reassignable function buttons. The rear touchscreen has twice the resolution of the old M10, though if you&#8217;re a real Leica fan you&#8217;ll probably have your eye to the optical finder.<\/p>\n<p>Interestingly, but controversially, the M11 uses its full sensor at all times for exposure purposes. Having the camera essentially always in &#8220;live view&#8221; mode means accurate exposures, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.dpreview.com\/reviews\/leica-m11-initial-review\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">but according to DPReview&#8217;s initial review<\/a>, it leads to longish startup times \u2014 and Leicas are generally quick as lightning to turn on and shoot with.<\/p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a USB-C port that charges the camera&#8217;s new and much larger battery, or to pull shots off the card or 64-gig internal memory \u2014 or to suck them directly onto your phone and a companion app (another reason not to shoot full rez).<\/p>\n<p>Leica&#8217;s M series is unique and definitely not an option for more hobby photographers, who will rightfully balk at the $8,995 price for the M11 body \u2014 the M10 debuted at $6,600 in 2017, and even adjusting for inflation the new price is eye-popping. And of course that&#8217;s before you get any lenses!<\/p>\n<p>But the point is not to recommend this camera specifically \u2014 more to note that Leica is still making technically interesting and quite competent cameras, the technology of which occasionally dips down to prices that mere mortals like you and I might be able to afford (after living on ramen for a month or two, anyway). Expect to see more variants of the M11 over the years, but also some of the design lessons on display here applied to something more affordable. Not <em>affordable<\/em> affordable, but &#8220;less than a used car&#8221; affordable.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Leica&#8217;s a strange one. It only puts out a handful of cameras every year, and most of them are remixes or minor iterations on previous models. Since 2017 its flagship has been the solid but still somewhat archaic M10, but now the company has revealed its successor: the even more solid and also still somewhat g":"leica","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/304554"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=304554"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=304554"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=304554"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=304554"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":436,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/photography\/","name":"Photography","slug":"photography","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/436"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=436"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=436"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=436"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=436"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2254886,"date":"2022-01-07T13:23:45","date_gmt":"2022-01-07T21:23:45","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2254886"},"modified":"2022-01-09T13:39:01","modified_gmt":"2022-01-09T21:39:01","slug":"ces-2022-best-weirdest-car-tech","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/07\/ces-2022-best-weirdest-car-tech\/","title":{"rendered":"The best (and weirdest) future car tech at CES 2022"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Another virtual year<\/span> at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/\">CES 2022<\/a> is in the bag for TechCrunch, and even though we attended the event remotely, one thing in the vehicle space was made abundantly clear: Your car is about so much more than mobility. In fact, if you think a vehicle is about getting you from point A to point B, think again, peasant!<\/p>\n<p>Your car \u2014 at least in the eyes of automakers and tech companies \u2014 is a third space, a place where you can work or lounge or watch TV. It\u2019s a device, connecting you with the other devices that run your life. It\u2019s an assistant, anticipating your needs by creepily watching you and collecting data on your every movement.<\/p>\n<p>The big themes this year focused on services and experiences that drivers and passengers can have inside vehicles, the advanced driver-assistance systems (ADAS) and automated driving features that handle some of the drudgery of driving so you can have those experiences, and the compute power needed to deliver it all.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2254886\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Of course, there was other vehicle tech that popped up: Who can forget BMW\u2019s color-changing car? NFTs even made an appearance. Here\u2019s the in-vehicle tech that stood out to us.<\/p>\n<h2>Compute power for the win<\/h2>\n<p>We heard a lot about digital cockpits that transform the front cab into a world of digital content, entertainment and services. Many companies threw around the term \u201cco-pilot\u201d and depending on how that company defined it, the co-pilot could include voice assistants or even actual driver-assistance systems that can control certain functions of the vehicles. And there were deep insinuations that one should never, if one can help it, stop watching TV or streaming video \u2014 especially not when in a moving vehicle.<\/p>\n<p>All of that requires processing power and at 2022 CES the automotive chip game was on.<\/p>\n<h3>Qualcomm\u2019s Snapdragon Digital Chassis<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2252834\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2252834\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2252834\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png\" alt=\"Qualcomm's Snapdragon Digital Chassis render showing advanced connected infotainment system in vehicle\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png 1920w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Snapdragon-Digital-Chassis-Render-03.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2252834\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Qualcomm Technologies<\/p><\/div><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Qualcomm doubled down on its commitment to powering <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/qualcomm-ces-auto-snapdragon-digital-chassis\/\">automotive in-vehicle tech<\/a> at CES 2022 by bringing on new OEM clients. The tech giant\u2019s Snapdragon Digital Chassis offers automakers a platter of cloud-connected \u201cplatforms\u201d consisting of systems on a chip (SoC) and software that can be adopted in full or \u00e0 la carte.<\/p>\n<p>The chassis includes: the Snapdragon Ride Platform for ADAS and automated driving, the Auto Connectivity Platform for LTE, 5G connected services, cellular vehicle-to-everything (C-V2X), Wi-Fi, Bluetooth and precise positioning, and the next generation of the Snapdragon Cockpit, a digital cockpit and infotainment system.<\/p>\n<p>Volvo and Honda announced plans to integrate the digital cockpit into upcoming electric vehicles, and Renault, which has already committed to bringing the cockpit into future cars, expanded the partnership to include everything the chassis has to offer. General Motors will also be relying on Snapdragon to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/gm-taps-qualcomm-to-power-new-hands-free-driver-assistance-starting-with-cadillac\/\">power its next-gen ADAS<\/a>.<\/p>\n<h3>Nvidia\u2019s Drive Orin SoC<\/h3>\n<p>While Volvo\u2019s infotainment is being powered by Qualcomm\u2019s SoC, its new automated driving (AD) features will be powered by Nvidia\u2019s. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/tusimple-integrates-nvidias-newest-auto-grade-chip-to-scale-autonomous-trucking\/\">Autonomous trucking startup TuSimple also said at CES 2022<\/a> that it would use Drive Orin to power and scale its self-driving tech.<\/p>\n<p>Nvidia\u2019s chip is a central computer for intelligent vehicles that\u2019s made specifically for autonomous applications. It delivers 254 trillion operations per seconds and provides the sort of auto-grade compute power needed to handle self-driving functions.<\/p>\n<p>JiDU Auto, Baidu&#8217;s electric vehicle company, also announced it will use the Nvidia Drive Orin SoC. This next-generation vehicle with Level 4 autonomous driving capability will make its debut at the Beijing Auto Show in April, followed by mass production and delivery by 2023.<\/p>\n<p>Other companies using Drive Orin include\u00a0Polestar, IM Motors, Li Auto, NIO, R Auto and Xpeng.<\/p>\n<h3>Intel-Mobileye<\/h3>\n<p>Intel subsidiary Mobileye announced plans to bring a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/04\/intels-mobileye-autonomous-driving-chip-for-consumer-vehicles\/\">new supercomputer<\/a> to market designed to give passenger cars, trucks and SUVs autonomous driving powers.<\/p>\n<p>The company introduced at the 2022 CES tech trade show a new system on chip called EyeQ Ultra that is purpose-built for autonomous driving. The company said the first silicon for the EyeQ Ultra SoC, which is capable of 176 trillion operations per second (TOPS), is expected at the end of 2023 with full automotive grade production in 2025.<\/p>\n<p>The company also introduced at CES its next-generation EyeQ SoC for advanced driver-assistance systems called EyeQ6L and EyeQ6H.<\/p>\n<h2>Connected everything<\/h2>\n<p>What do you get when you combine the internet with insane processing power in a vehicle? A sci-fi world of incredible, and some might say unnecessary, tech that lets car owners sync their digital and physical worlds.<\/p>\n<p>Want to program your car to order you a pizza as you leave the office so it\u2019s hot and ready when you get home? It can be done. Feel like hearing the stats on your battery\u2019s power and vehicle range? Speak and it shall be delivered. Want to put your feet up and watch the latest episode of \u201cThe Wheel of Time\u201d? There\u2019s tech for that, too.<\/p>\n<p>The in-vehicle tech displayed at CES drilled home the idea of the car as a connected device that is meant to make your life easier, smoother and more entertaining.<\/p>\n<h3>Google<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253607\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253607\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2253607\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png\" alt=\"Google Home device voice assist to heat up volvo car\" width=\"1024\" height=\"584\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png 2644w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=150,86 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=300,171 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=768,438 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=680,388 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=1536,876 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=2048,1168 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Screen-Shot-2022-01-05-at-6.25.18-pm.png?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253607\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Volvo Cars<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Many cars today run their infotainment systems off of Android\u2019s auto operating system, making it easier to access your phone and compatible apps on your phone from your car. This year, Google took it a few steps further.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/google-home-youtube-integrate-with-volvo-cars\/\">Volvo and Google announced an integration with the Google Home ecosystem<\/a>, which would allow Volvo car owners to issue voice commands to Google Assistant-enabled devices. They can tell the assistant to do things like turn the car on and off, heat it up or cool it down and provide car info like battery life. Volvo also shared plans to enable YouTube app downloads, thanks to both Google integrations with Volvo vehicles and Qualcomm\u2019s Snapdragon cockpit.<\/p>\n<p>Google also added features to its digital car key with BMW, which enables users to lock, unlock and start certain BMW cars with select Google Pixel and Samsung Galaxy phones. Now, the car will automatically unlock itself when the device gets close enough, and users can share their digital car key with friends or family.<\/p>\n<h3>Amazon<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253780\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253780\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2253780\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png\" alt=\"Amazon fire tv wheel of time\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png 1400w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/1_ArAPbCYor2lNl_StFr9pXA-1.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253780\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Amazon<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In previous years at CES, Amazon showed up in a number of vehicles via its virtual assistant Alexa. This year, the power of Alexa is combining with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/amazon-fire-tv-is-coming-to-more-cars-in-2022\/\">Amazon\u2019s Fire TV streaming platform<\/a>, which is working its way into more cars.<\/p>\n<p>Last year, global automaker Stellantis integrated the Fire TV into its vehicles, and at CES 2022, we\u2019re seeing the in-car entertainment systems of certain Jeep, Chrysler, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/bmw-wants-to-turn-your-car-into-a-rolling-cinema\/\">BMW<\/a> and Ford vehicles get an upgrade, as well.<\/p>\n<p>Fire TV for cars will do more than offer a TV streaming platform. It\u2019ll sync with Alexa so drivers and passengers can simply speak a command and <em>poof!<\/em>, \u201cOlaf Presents\u201d is playing in the backseat and your children are blessedly quiet. Users can also ask Alexa to show their Ring doorbell video on the Fire TV using voice commands.<\/p>\n<p>Stellantis is getting even cozier with Amazon. At CES 2022, Stellantis <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/stellantis-draft\/\">announced a wide-ranging collaboration<\/a> that will touch nearly every aspect of its business. Amazon&#8217;s technology will be used to help Stellantis develop vehicles, build connected in-vehicle experiences and train the next generation of automotive software engineers.<\/p>\n<p>As part of this multiyear deal, Stellantis has selected Amazon Web Services (AWS) as its preferred cloud provider for vehicle platforms. Stellantis, which recently launched a software academy for existing and new employees, is also working with AWS to create a curriculum that will cover software, data and cloud technology.<\/p>\n<h3>Cerence<\/h3>\n<p>Software company Cerence unveiled its Cerence Co-Pilot, an in-car assistant that uses continuous learning to anticipate the needs of drivers and proactively initiate actions. The co-pilot is integrated with the car\u2019s sensors and data to understand the environment inside the vehicle and around it, analyzing things like voice, gaze, gesture and touch to understand user preferences and perform actions on the driver\u2019s behalf.<\/p>\n<p>Cerence\u2019s co-pilot can do things like control smart home and IoT devices, authorize payments for in-car purchases and remind drivers about car maintenance needs, even scheduling a trip to the shop for them.<\/p>\n<p>At CES, Cerence announced a partnership to introduce this tech to Vietnamese automaker Vinfast&#8217;s cars (more on that below). No other integrations were shared, but a <a href=\"https:\/\/vimeo.com\/657534151\/4e8916fe3b\">video<\/a> demonstrating the tech showed such brands as Volvo, BMW, Audi and Mercedes, some of which have worked with Cerence in the past.<\/p>\n<h3>Blackberry<\/h3>\n<p>Blackberry announced a partnership with Pateo, an internet-of-vehicles service and product provider in China, that will see Blackberry Ivy, the company\u2019s intelligent vehicle data platform co-developed with Amazon Web Services, integrated into Pateo\u2019s digital cockpit solution. The two companies are to work with an unnamed Chinese automaker to pilot the cockpit on its electric model lineup.<\/p>\n<p>The software company most renowned for its mobile phones didn\u2019t share much about what that cockpit would look like, but it should encompass such features as intelligent voice, entertainment, vehicle health monitoring, secure payment and cloud technology. Blackberry and Pateo will also incorporate Electra Vehicles\u2019s EVE-Ai 360 Adaptive Controls that provides prediction of battery state of charge, state of health and project vehicle range.<\/p>\n<h2>ADAS\/AD<\/h2>\n<p>In past years, autonomous driving took center stage. This year, the focus was more on advanced driver-assistance systems and promises to bring restricted automated driving features to passenger vehicles. Due to the advancements in vehicle sensors, compute power and software, automakers are working to automate certain aspects of the car, like parking or highway driving.<\/p>\n<p>That doesn\u2019t mean some companies pursuing so-called Level 4 autonomous driving didn\u2019t show up at CES; they just weren\u2019t the ones yelling the loudest this year.<\/p>\n<h3>GM\u2019s Ultra Cruise<\/h3>\n<p>As we mentioned earlier, GM\u2019s new Ultra Cruise hands-free ADAS system will be powered by Qualcomm\u2019s Snapdragon SoC. GM introduced the Ultra Cruise system in 2021, but this was the first time we heard more details about the compute and some of the capabilities.<\/p>\n<p>The system is an upgrade from the automaker\u2019s Super Cruise ADAS first introduced in 2017, and it\u2019s expected to be able to handle 95% of all driving scenarios.<\/p>\n<p>Ultra Cruise, which is coming to the new electric Cadillac Celestiq in 2023, will rely on sensors like cameras, radar and lidar (not just lidar map data) to feed data to GM\u2019s software that will then output decisions.<\/p>\n<h3>Volvo\u2019s Ride Pilot<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253530\" style=\"width: 953px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253530\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2253530\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png\" alt=\"Volvo Cars Concept Recharge showing autonomous vehicle using lidar\" width=\"943\" height=\"363\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png 943w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png?resize=150,58 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png?resize=300,115 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png?resize=768,296 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png?resize=680,262 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/292920_Volvo_Cars_Concept_Recharge_safety_illustration.png?resize=50,19 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 943px) 100vw, 943px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253530\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Volvo Cars<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Volvo shared plans to work with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/volvo-partners-with-luminar-and-zenseact-to-bring-autonomous-driving-feature-to-new-e-suv\/\">lidar company Luminar<\/a> and AD software company Zenseact to introduce Ride Pilot as an add-on subscription to an electric SUV that will be revealed later this year. Ride Pilot is an \u201cunsupervised\u201d AD feature, meaning it can drive itself fully while drivers are on certain highways, giving them the ability to go completely hands and eyes free so they can enjoy other activities, like the YouTube watching we mentioned earlier.<\/p>\n<h3>JiDU<\/h3>\n<p>Chinese internet giant Baidu\u2019s EV startup JiDU came to CES 2022 with news that it would power its first production EV model, which is expected to begin deliveries in 2023, on Nvidia\u2019s Drive Orin SoC (as mentioned above). The company said it would have Level 4 autonomous driving capabilities, all of which would be revealed in April at the Beijing Auto Show.<\/p>\n<p>JiDu is just a year old and recently demonstrated intelligent assisted driving in both urban and high-speed areas in its SIMUCar.<\/p>\n<h3>Cadillac<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254175\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254175\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2254175\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg\" alt=\"Cadillac autonomous lounge concept innerspace\" width=\"1024\" height=\"683\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg 2000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=1536,1025 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/9811cff0-6e61-11ec-b1bf-cde05721dd38.cf_.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254175\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Cadillac<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>While not entirely focused on autonomous driving capabilities or ADAS features, it\u2019s worth noting how <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/cadillacs-new-self-driving-concept-is-a-luxury-loveseat-on-wheels\/\">Cadillac envisions the inside of its future autonomous vehicles<\/a>. Its InnerSpace concept shows your standard spaceship-looking two-seater car from the outside, while inside it still looks like a spaceship. But like a sexy spaceship.<\/p>\n<p>Rather than separate driver and passenger seats, there\u2019s a plush and sleek loveseat that appears to constantly be in recline mode, which checks out given the built-in ottoman and compartment for slippers and a blanket. A mere couple of feet in front of the passengers\u2019 heads is a wide, curved screen. No steering wheels or pedals are featured.<\/p>\n<h3>Indy Autonomous Challenge<\/h3>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/racer1.gif\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout alignnone wp-image-2255223 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/racer1.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"422\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n<p>Last October, teams from around the world converged on the Indianapolis Motor Speedway to demonstrate autonomous racing.<\/p>\n<p>The teams gathered again, this time at the Las Vegas Motor Speedway on January 7 with the Autonomous Challenge @ CES. IAC university teams developed the software that runs the autonomous racecar, the Dallara AV-21.<\/p>\n<p>Leading up to the event, the organization published a few videos, including this <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=uVF_JVhOrU4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one that was filmed at night<\/a>.<\/p>\n<h3>Gentex<\/h3>\n<p>Gentex, which supplies automotive and aerospace sectors, showed off the results of two acquisitions in 2021: Israel-based Guardian Optical Technologies and Vaposens.<\/p>\n<p>The company showed a lot, but its ultra-sensitive driver monitoring system that is designed to be used to support driver-assistance systems got our attention. Guardian Optical Technologies developed an infrared-sensitive, high-resolution camera combining machine vision, depth perception and micro-vibration detection. What this means is its proprietary sensor configuration can monitor the entire vehicle cabin and all its objects and occupants, assessing their behavior, gestures and activities.<\/p>\n<h2>NFTs, color changing cars and other fun stuff<\/h2>\n<h3>Vinfast<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2255174\" style=\"width: 1610px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2255174\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2255174 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg\" alt=\"Vinfast CES 2022 electric vehicles\" width=\"1600\" height=\"1066\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=1536,1023 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/S9.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2255174\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Vinfast<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>In addition to revealing three new EVs at CES this year, Vietnamese EV company Vinfast announced the formation of its early-bird reservation site. The first to preorder will receive a \u201cVinFirst\u201d certificate on the blockchain platform in NFT form, which the company says is a completely transparent way to prove ownership of an order number.<\/p>\n<p>The term &#8220;digital twin&#8221; popped up a few times in the automotive sector at CES 2022, including an announcement from Cerence and Vinfast. The gist is this: Cerence has cloud-based software that allows Vinfast (or any other company intrigued by the product) to create a virtual representation of its entire car, including software, mechanics, electrics and physical behavior, along with driver data and environmental data.<\/p>\n<h3>Indi EV<\/h3>\n<p>Indi EV, a California-based EV startup, came out with a prototype of its Indi One at CES, which the company says is \u201cthe world\u2019s first social media-oriented car.\u201d What that seems to mean is a car that has an integrated computer for gaming, a complete Windows workstation that can handle Zoom calls and even record events that can later be shared on social media and software that lets riders capture trip content and video to be uploaded to the cloud.<\/p>\n<p>If all that wasn\u2019t enough, the Indi One is meant to enable a type of mobile blockchain, wherein each vehicle can act as a node for a blockchain. Exactly why that\u2019s significant is unclear, but You Do You, Indi EV. Customers can start preordering by the end of Q1, and the car is expected to go for around $45,000.<\/p>\n<h3>BMW<\/h3>\n<p>BMW <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/bmw-shows-off-a-color-changing-car\/\">unwrapped its color-changing car at CES, the BMW iX Flow<\/a>. Right now, the e-paper wrapping the vehicle can only change between black and white, but more colors are expected in the future that will enable users to give their car a more personalized look to match their mood.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253428\" style=\"width: 810px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/bmw_flow.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253428\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2253428 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/bmw_flow.gif\" alt=\"BMW color changing car CES 2022 \" width=\"800\" height=\"364\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253428\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> BMW<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: aktiv-grotesk, sans-serif; letter-spacing: -0.02em; font-size: 1rem;\">Nextbase<\/span>Dash cam tech company Nextbase unveiled its smart and connected dash cam, the Nextbase iQ. It gives drivers a lot of the same safety and security features they would get in their home-monitoring systems, like real-time alerts and access to incident video even while they\u2019re away from their car. Users can also get real-time access to the dash cam from anywhere at anytime through the iQ app.<\/p>\n<h3>Mercedes-Benz<\/h3>\n<p>Finally, Mercedes revealed the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/03\/mercedes-benzs-vision-for-the-future-is-an-ultra-efficient-luxury-620-mile-range-ev\/\">Vision EQXX<\/a>, a concept vehicle that is meant to showcase what the automaker&#8217;s electric future will look like. This eye-popping sport EV wasn&#8217;t just about aerodynamics and a sleek design. The company squeezed in power, efficiency and range into the compact and sporty package.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2252520\" style=\"width: 2010px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2252520\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2252520 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg\" alt=\"Mercedes-Benz VISION EQXX CES\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1250\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg 2000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=150,94 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=300,188 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=768,480 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=680,425 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=1536,960 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/2021-12-21_Image_22C0001-067.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2000px) 100vw, 2000px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2252520\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Mercedes-Benz reveals the VISION EQXX interior. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Mercedes-Benz<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Some of the neat tech in the EQXX worth noting is the\u00a0one-piece 47.5-inch LED display with 8K resolution. The infotainment screen has responsive real-time graphics that will span the width of the vehicle, according to Mercedes.<\/p>\n<p>The automaker worked with NAVIS Automotive Systems to develop a 3D navigation system that users can zoom into and scroll around for this massive screen. And like the company&#8217;s newer models, the EQXX also featured an advanced voice assistant and software that learns your behavior over time.<\/p>\n<h2>Lidar companies try to make a concrete value prop<\/h2>\n<p>In the lidar world, Luminar&#8217;s eyebrow-raising stunt comparing Tesla&#8217;s ADAS system to its own (to the peril of several child-size dummies) was affecting, and its inclusion in Volvo vehicles and Mobileye systems is a coup. But it&#8217;s still an expensive and complex system, a major investment with uncertain (if potentially significant) benefits.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Here\u2019s me driving the Tesla Model Y on the left. It, of course, doesn\u2019t have LiDAR. On the right is the <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/luminartech?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@luminartech<\/a> enabled vehicle. <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/search?q=%24LAZR&amp;src=ctag&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">$LAZR<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/FlQVlQcw8O\">pic.twitter.com\/FlQVlQcw8O<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Patrick Moorhead attended #CES2022 in-person (@PatrickMoorhead) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/PatrickMoorhead\/status\/1478766165723779077?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 5, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Manufacturers are struggling to produce something that creates a useful outcome for a vehicle at a reasonable price. Costs haven&#8217;t come down as much as they&#8217;d like, and there&#8217;s still confusion over who does what in a perception stack.<\/p>\n<p>Blickfeld is attempting to take over as much as possible, for instance, with on-device movement detection, object classification and so on, which could make their devices easier to drop in \u2014 or possibly make them partially redundant with an already intelligent in-car computer vision system.<\/p>\n<p>Arbe is focusing more narrowly on what it calls &#8220;free space mapping,&#8221; where it doesn&#8217;t matter if it&#8217;s a bush or a raccoon or what \u2014 the question is, is it safe to drive on? A quick, dedicated sensor for identifying driveable surfaces in the vicinity could be a useful feature and one that contributes to the autonomous vehicle collective intelligence.<\/p>\n<p>Innoviz is improving on the traditional spinning puck lidar type, which has proven to be useful in many circumstances. A cheaper, better version may find success where trailblazer Velodyne has over the years.<\/p>\n<p>Similarly, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/30\/voyant-raises-15m-to-scale-production-of-its-tiny-inexpensive-lidar-tech\/\">Voyant Photonics<\/a> is leaving the whole automotive market to deeper pockets, focusing on producing its tiny, inexpensive lidar unit for robotics and industrial applications, where certifications and liabilities aren&#8217;t quite so intense.<\/p>\n<p>There&#8217;s no doubt lidar has a future in autonomous vehicles and other equipment, but what form it will take and how much people will pay for it \u2014 that&#8217;s still very much up in the air, something that no doubt makes everyone in the sector a little nervous.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/?utm_source=internal&amp;utm_medium=footer-banner\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/12\/ces-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about CES 2022 on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Another virtual year at CES 2022 is in the bag for TechCrunch, and even though we attended the event remotely, one thing in the vehicle space was made abundantly clear: Your car is about so much more than mobility. DRIVE Orin","slug":"nvidia-drive-orin","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576966684"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576966684"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576966684"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576966684"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576966684"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":182541,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/qualcomm\/","name":"Qualcomm","slug":"qualcomm","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/182541"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=182541"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=182541"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=182541"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=182541"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2254184,"date":"2022-01-06T09:41:00","date_gmt":"2022-01-06T17:41:00","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2254184"},"modified":"2022-01-06T13:35:59","modified_gmt":"2022-01-06T21:35:59","slug":"look-upon-my-ces-2022-work-from-home-setup-and-despair","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/06\/look-upon-my-ces-2022-work-from-home-setup-and-despair\/","title":{"rendered":"Look upon my CES 2022 work from home setup and despair"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Working from home has been my normal for more than a decade, but it&#8217;s getting a bit stale. Time to spice it up \u2014 with some of CES 2022&#8217;s hottest items, all of which definitely kind of exist.<\/p>\n<p>First off let&#8217;s upgrade these dinky twin 27-inch Dells I&#8217;ve been attempting to work on for the last couple years. They&#8217;re flat \u2014 lifeless! And the bezels between them? So disorientating! What I need is something I can just stick my head right in and be <em>immersed<\/em> in the TechCrunch experience.<\/p>\n<p>Samsung knows what&#8217;s up: one giant 55-inch monitor curved like a snow shovel. <a href=\"https:\/\/news.samsung.com\/global\/samsung-electronics-unveils-together-for-tomorrow-vision-at-ces-2022\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Odyssey Ark<\/a> is an experiment in next-gen media, meant for you to be streaming, gaming and video chatting all at the same time on the same screen. Check out how it dominates YouTuber Tim Schofield:<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2254184\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Here is a first look at the INSANE Odyssey Ark from <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Samsung?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Samsung<\/a>! This is a curved 55&quot; 4K Monitor with a 16:9 aspect ratio&#8230; Can do some serious gaming\/multitasking on this! <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/ces?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#ces<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/samsung?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#samsung<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/Y82hbeY9gg\">pic.twitter.com\/Y82hbeY9gg<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Tim Schofield (@qbking77) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/qbking77\/status\/1478555909068505088?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">January 5, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Now if I&#8217;m going to have to tip backwards about 40 degrees to read the top of the PDF I display at 750% on there (ever print a document that big? That text is <em>crisp<\/em>), I better have a decent chair. Fortunately Razer&#8217;s got my back \u2014 literally.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/press.razer.com\/product-news\/ces-2022-project-sophia-enkiprohs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Enki Pro HyperSense<\/a> isn&#8217;t just a comfy chair I can easily dominate Halo: Infinite deathmatches from. It&#8217;s basically a giant Rumble Pak.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254201\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254201\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254201\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg\" alt=\"Rendering of the mechanical interior of the Razer Enki hypersense chair.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"732\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg 1354w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg?resize=150,107 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg?resize=300,214 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg?resize=768,549 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg?resize=680,486 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/enki-chair.jpg?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254201\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Razer<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;With 65,000 haptic variations it has the tactile feedback of +\/- 1 G-Force and can create 1.5 inches of vertical and backward tilt in your seat,&#8221; Razer explains. So when your Warthog gets naded, you don&#8217;t just feel it in your pride, you actually fall over as your chair bounces you up and out. Well, maybe you won&#8217;t fall, but if you&#8217;re streaming it&#8217;ll get a laugh, so lean into it.<\/p>\n<p>I&#8217;ve got to work while I play, though, so I need a keyboard that matches the quality of my writing. Writing really starts from the <em>keys<\/em>, as I&#8217;ve always said. Why do you think all the old-style authors had those great chunky typewriters? Can&#8217;t write cool characters if you don&#8217;t look cool doing it. I&#8217;m not sure how Neal Stephenson gets around that.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254214\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254214\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254214\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg\" alt=\"A Keychron keyboard seen from above.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"457\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg 1720w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=150,67 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=300,134 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=768,342 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=680,303 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=1536,685 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/q1-keychron.jpg?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254214\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Keychron<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>But every writing style is different, and you should build your keyboard from the ground up and with a good foundation. That&#8217;s Keychron&#8217;s Q1 for you: solid as hell, and you can assemble it yourself with a bunch of different styles of keycaps and switches on tap. Why not have WASD in gaming linear but the rest in clicky tactile? Well, probably because it&#8217;ll feel weird, but you get the idea.<\/p>\n<p>(Joking aside, I actually have one of these to test and it&#8217;s pretty nice. A good mechanical keyboard is a perfectly practical way to upgrade your own WFH setup.)<\/p>\n<p>What&#8217;s that keyboard plugged into? Glad you asked. See, I&#8217;ve come to understand that heat management is at the core of PC performance, but at the same time good insulation is at the core of a quiet rig. How can I have both, though? And don&#8217;t say liquid cooling! That&#8217;s just crazy. No, I&#8217;m going with the most elaborate solution possible.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254220\" style=\"width: 650px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/holecase-1.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254220\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254220\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/holecase-1.gif\" alt=\"Animation of a PC case with vents opening on the front.\" width=\"640\" height=\"589\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254220\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> CyberPowerPC<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.cyberpowerpc.com\/page\/ces-2022\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Kinetic series from CyberPowerPC<\/a> uses a complex set of folding triangles to produce variable airflow across the face of the case, opening and closing as heat requirements change. Why triangles? Why this origami style and not just some valves? Why such a complex arrangement doomed to get clogged with dust? Hello, because it looks awesome.<\/p>\n<p>I know what you&#8217;re thinking. How will people see all my important swag when I&#8217;m on a video call? First of all, thanks for your concern, I appreciate it. You&#8217;re a kind person. But I thought of that too. Check out my new Zoom setup:<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254227\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254227\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254227\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg\" alt=\"A life-sized image of a person on a video screen doing a video call.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"686\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg 2694w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=150,101 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=300,201 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=768,515 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=680,456 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=1536,1030 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=2048,1373 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/lavitre-stage.jpg?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254227\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> LaVitre<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Right?!<\/p>\n<p>Not only will they see my whole tasteful computing nook, but also how I&#8217;m&#8230; definitely fully dressed in professional clothes during the workday. Okay, maybe I can angle it so&#8230; well, I&#8217;ll figure it out. Anyway, this huge telepresence rig <a href=\"https:\/\/lavitre.fr\/en-us\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">comes from French company la Vitre<\/a>, which advertises it as &#8220;an 86-inch experience.&#8221; It&#8217;s actually got a bunch of other cool stuff built in too.<\/p>\n<p>Lastly, I need to make sure I&#8217;ve got the freshest ping in the lobby or people will think when I dodge their shots it&#8217;s all down to packet loss. TP-Link has the final word with its <a href=\"https:\/\/www.tp-link.com\/us\/home-networking\/wifi-router\/archer-axe200-omni\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Archer AXE200 Omni robotic router<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254232\" style=\"width: 650px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/roborouter.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254232\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254232\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/roborouter.gif\" alt=\"Animation of a router automatically moving its antennas.\" width=\"640\" height=\"527\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254232\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> TP-Link<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>No more getting up and going to the router to tweak your antenna configuration. Wait&#8230; you don&#8217;t do that? No wonder you aren&#8217;t climbing the leaderboard, my friend. Signal goblins. Just wait for this thing to come out and it&#8217;ll take care of everything for you. After the robocalypse, every one of the hunter-killers will cold sport one of these bad boys.<\/p>\n<p>Right, there&#8217;s my big upgrade. I&#8217;m sure I&#8217;ll have all the pieces here in person some time in the next decade or so.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/?utm_source=internal&amp;utm_medium=footer-banner\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/12\/ces-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about CES 2022 on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Working from home has been my normal for more than a decade, but it&#8217;s getting a bit stale. efield-companies?tags=32518"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=32518"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=32518"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":759569,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tp-link\/","name":"tp-link","slug":"tp-link","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/759569"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=759569"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=759569"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=759569"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=759569"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576746957,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/work-from-home\/","name":"Work From Home","slug":"work-from-home","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576746957"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576746957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576746957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576746957"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576746957"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2253251,"date":"2022-01-05T09:53:14","date_gmt":"2022-01-05T17:53:14","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2253251"},"modified":"2022-01-06T14:51:54","modified_gmt":"2022-01-06T22:51:54","slug":"new-pet-tech-at-ces-treats-dogs-and-cats-like-the-complex-beings-they-are","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/new-pet-tech-at-ces-treats-dogs-and-cats-like-the-complex-beings-they-are\/","title":{"rendered":"New pet tech at CES treats dogs and cats like the complex beings they are"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">There&#8217;s always fun tech for pet owners at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/\">CES<\/a>, and 2022 is no different. But a handful of gadgets this year are taking care to treat dogs and cats not just as beloved furry friends but as intelligent animals with their own processes, emotions and even a desire to express themselves.<\/p>\n<p>At the most basic level \u2014 which is to say, pretty advanced compared with a few years ago \u2014 we have <strong><a href=\"https:\/\/rabo.cat\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Catlog<\/a><\/strong>, a smart cat collar and weight-sensing platform that helps owners keep track of their feline&#8217;s daily movements.<\/p>\n<p>The collar senses movement and vibrations, which it correlates with &#8220;cat-like behavior&#8221; like sleeping, sitting there, washing its paws, eating and drinking \u2014 even moving around, which some cats have been known to do. All these actions (including hairballs) gets sent to you through an IoT hub nearly live. And you can look back over your cat&#8217;s day to see when and how often they&#8217;ve played, slept and so on.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2253251\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>This basic aspect of illuminating a pet&#8217;s daily life when you&#8217;re not around is a good first step to understanding that they are more than a lap accessory \u2014 they exist and do things even when you&#8217;re not looking.<\/p>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/Ksne8tpBsvE?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p><strong>Invoxia<\/strong> takes things a little further with its smart collar that tracks your dog&#8217;s location but also its heart and respiratory condition. Now, I can&#8217;t vouch for the efficacy of this, but given the advances we&#8217;ve made in smart watches and other devices that can detect adverse events or conditions in humans, it doesn&#8217;t seem implausible at all that something similar could be whipped up for dogs.<\/p>\n<p>Animals have heart and lung issues just like any other animal with those organs, and sadly some breeds are predisposed to them as well. Sure, you can take them to the vet twice a year so she can listen to the dog&#8217;s breathing, but why not also have a collar that alerts you if something seems off? Just like with ourselves, an ounce of prevention is worth a pound of cure.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253370\" style=\"width: 982px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253370\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2253370\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg\" alt=\"Three different size dogs wear Inupathy heart rate detecting backpacks.\" width=\"972\" height=\"562\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg 972w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg?resize=150,87 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg?resize=300,173 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg?resize=768,444 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg?resize=680,393 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/inupathy.jpg?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 972px) 100vw, 972px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253370\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Inupathy<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Beyond just detecting physiological signs we find <strong><a href=\"https:\/\/www.inupathy.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inupathy<\/a><\/strong>, a dog-worn backpack that the company claims can detect a variety of psychological conditions as well. Now, let us not give too much credit here, as human-focused devices along these lines have had very mixed results as well. But Langualess, which makes the backpack, <a href=\"https:\/\/langualess.com\/#tech\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">explains their work as follows<\/a>:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>An animal&#8217;s heart normally beats at a gentle rhythm, but accelerates when the animal starts feeling nervous. This change in the rhythm is triggered by the sympathetic nervous activity. Through our independent research, we have found that it is possible to estimate the dogs\u2019 mental state in more detail by analysing the heart rate variability in depth.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Heart rate analysis is of course a field with a long and rich history, and one with as many hits as misses. But it is not unreasonable to think that you can tell whether a dog is relaxed, temporarily excited, or entering a prolonged angry or anxious state. The company&#8217;s main tech advance has been to create a local sensor and circuit that reliably detects and characterizes the animal&#8217;s heart rate.<\/p>\n<p>There are of course more external tells, like tail position, stance and vocalizations, but not every dog is so emotive and anyway, why not add a little more data to the mix?<\/p>\n<p>A propos additional data, Taiwan&#8217;s largest applied research institution ITRI showed off its neat <strong>iPetWeaR<\/strong> concept, which goes deep on data-driven early warning signals for doggie heart attack prevention. The low-power physiological detection radar technology is harmless &#8211; it does not require skin contact with the pet &#8211; and can be attached to a pet&#8217;s collar or stuffed into a doggie bed for flexible sensing.<\/p>\n<p>The basic US$80 product package includes a sensor device, a collar selected from various options, and a mobile app &#8211; and works for both cats and dogs.\u00a0The company put together an adorable demo video, which of course an excellent reason for us to include it in our roundup:<\/p>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/GUHGec_9sCI?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The physiological data collected by the iPetWear is scooped up and beamed to the pet owner&#8217;s phone by Bluetooth. In the case of irregular heartbeat or breathing, a notification is sent so the owner can intervene &#8211; and the product promises early detection of a pet\u2019s underlying health condition.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/wagz.com\/\"><strong>Wagz<\/strong><\/a> has been around for a hot minute, and its Freedom Collar introduced virtual geofences so you can ensure your four-legged friends stays put. With GPS tracking, fitness mapping and &#8216;humane&#8217; corrections (as opposed to a shock collar), the collar has become a popular solution for training pups. New for CES 2022, though, is the addition of Wagz Tagz. The idea is letting the dog roam free around the house, but creating small zones where the pup isn&#8217;t allowed. When the collar gets too close to a Wagz Tag, it triggers the geofencing. A great &#8211; and super clever &#8211; way of keeping Fido off the furniture.<\/p>\n<p>The Wagz Tagz let you create customizable Keep Out Zones from 3 ft to 15 ft to keep your pet safe and away from areas you want to protect.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2254223\" style=\"width: 1010px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2254223\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2254223\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1000\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg 1000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/Wagz_Contact.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2254223\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Wagz<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>While we&#8217;re at it, why not let the dog straight-up talk to you? <a href=\"https:\/\/fluent.pet\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">That&#8217;s the idea with <strong>FluentPet<\/strong><\/a>, which makes a set of buttons for teaching your dog to express itself using human vocabulary. Kind of.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253371\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253371\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2253371\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg\" alt=\"A dog's paws press buttons that emit words.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"684\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg 1600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=768,513 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=1536,1025 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/FluentPet-Buttons.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253371\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> FluentPet<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Clearly inspired by the social media stardom of button-expressing canines <a href=\"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/hunger4words\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stella<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/whataboutbunny\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bunny<\/a>, whose seemingly coherent utterances suggest a richer than expected intellectual landscape, the FluentPet buttons are an easy way to see if your dog is similarly gifted. (Let&#8217;s be honest \u2014 all dogs are good, but not all of them can reliably form sentences.)<\/p>\n<p>The various kits contain self-contained and labeled buttons that, when pressed, produce a word like &#8220;outside,&#8221; &#8220;food&#8221; or of course &#8220;love you.&#8221; These stick into larger, easily identifiable foam mats (hopefully they don&#8217;t taste good) to aid learning by sight.<\/p>\n<p>Does the dog really know what it means when it says &#8220;love you&#8221;? Perhaps, perhaps not \u2014 the love is not in doubt, but it may understand that when it presses that one, it gets pets. Likewise, the food button tends to speed up dinner. And pressing &#8220;outside&#8221; works faster than staring wistfully at the door. You may not be carrying on full conversations with the dog, but it could be a fun way to change up the way your best friend expresses themselves \u2014 because they certainly do that, and sometimes in regrettable ways.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/?utm_source=internal&amp;utm_medium=footer-banner\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/12\/ces-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about CES 2022 on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>There&#8217;s always fun tech for pet owners at CES, and 2022 is no different. But a handful of gadgets this year are taking care to treat dogs and cats not just as beloved furry friends but as intelligent animals with their own processes, emotions and even a desire to express themselves. At the most basic
