ef":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=9277"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=9277"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2253408,"date":"2022-01-05T05:01:45","date_gmt":"2022-01-05T13:01:45","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2253408"},"modified":"2022-01-05T09:57:28","modified_gmt":"2022-01-05T17:57:28","slug":"with-8m-seed-round-protai-leverages-the-proteome-to-speed-up-drug-discovery","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/05\/with-8m-seed-round-protai-leverages-the-proteome-to-speed-up-drug-discovery\/","title":{"rendered":"With $8M seed round, Protai leverages the proteome to speed up drug discovery"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Tech is an increasingly important part of the complex drug discovery and testing process, and with advances in processing power and algorithms it is tapping new areas for analysis. Proteomics, the domain of proteins and their interactions, is up next, and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protai.bio\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Protai<\/a> is one startup getting to work on it after raising an $8 million seed round.<\/p>\n<p>Diseases cause a variety of phenomena in the body, at various levels of organization. Say a disease causes cell death in the liver \u2014 why? Because cells are producing too much of this compound. Why? Because the inhibitor molecules don&#8217;t bind to the proteins that activate the production mechanism. Why? Because the RNA coding the protein has been damaged. Why? And so on.<\/p>\n<p>Where Protai fits into that stack is above the genome and transcription level, where genetic factors can be identified, and below the cells and systems layer, where problems become more obviously visible as symptoms.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2253408\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>To start, the company put together what it claims is the largest proteomic database, some 50,000 samples from 6,000 papers, and harmonized the chaotic data (natural language AI was helpful here) so it can act as a single source of information.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The idea is that instead of analyzing a small sample study, you want to analyze all of the data out there on a particular disease, but it\u2019s apples and oranges because proteins were collected and sequenced from a variety of conditions, instruments, protocols and controls,&#8221; explained CEO and co-founder Eran Seger.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253488\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253488\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2253488\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg\" alt=\"Illustration of layers of information in biotech, from genetic to molecular.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg 2500w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=2048,1153 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/protai-illo.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253488\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Protai<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>By putting them all together they can produce a higher-level &#8220;map&#8221; of proteins and their interactions in the context of a given disease. Knowing more about what&#8217;s happening at a molecular level is always good.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Our improvements in biological explainability give rise to better drug targets and drug candidates,&#8221; said Seger. &#8220;<span id=\"m_5192916589978083564gmail-docs-internal-guid-b3cf0267-7fff-1735-37ff-29a86bf6fe5e\">In our lung cancer proof of concept, we pinpointed several high-value targets that we are currently pursuing in our independent drug program, together with other markers that will help expand the use of known drugs into this indication.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253490\" style=\"width: 410px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253490\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2253490\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg\" alt=\"Protai co-founders Kirill Pevzner (left) and Eran Seger\" width=\"400\" height=\"396\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg 2000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=300,297 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=768,761 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=680,674 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=1536,1522 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/L-R-Kirill-Pevzner-and-Eran-Seger-Credit_-David-Garb.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253490\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Protai co-founders Kirill Pevzner (left) and Eran Seger. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Protai<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The company hopes to be able to span the drug discovery and testing process from tissue testing all the way to final clinical testing.<\/p>\n<p>A recent development in the proteomics world that may change how all this works is the use of AI-powered models to determine the structure and functionality of proteins generally known only by their signature sequence of amino acids.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/22\/deepmind-puts-the-entire-human-proteome-online-as-folded-by-alphafold\/\">DeepMind&#8217;s AlphaFold<\/a> and the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/22\/deepmind-puts-the-entire-human-proteome-online-as-folded-by-alphafold\/\">University of Washington&#8217;s RoseTTAfold<\/a> models are capable of accurately predicting the structure of proteins based on their sequence, something that was previously only possible with expensive lab testing. It&#8217;s shaking up entire disciplines that relied on the old methods.<\/p>\n<p>CTO and co-founder Kirill Prevzner said the advance is welcome: &#8220;We are integrating structural proteomics tools, such as AlphaFold, into our solution in two main ways. One is to further improve the prediction of protein-protein interactions. The second is in drug-target interactions. Both allow us to develop and optimize the best drug solutions for our targets.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The $8 million seed round, led by Grove Ventures and Pitango HealthTech, will go (as seed rounds often do) toward the development of the new platform and building out partnerships and other programs.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Tech is an increasingly important part of the complex drug discovery and testing process, and with advances in processing power and algorithms it is tapping new areas for analysis. Proteomics, the domain of proteins and their interactions, is up next, and Protai is one startup getting to work on it after raising an $8 million gives first details on next-gen PSVR2 headset for PS5"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Sony has announced some basic information about its much-anticipated next-generation VR hardware for the PS5, which it calls \u2014 predictably \u2014 PSVR2. Little was revealed about the device beyond its basic specs but it did confirm some features gamers will care about.<\/p>\n<p>The original PSVR was a competent, relatively affordable, easy to use device but fairly limited in terms of hardware: resolution, field of view and such. So Sony&#8217;s announcement that the new one will be considerably more advanced will be very welcome.<\/p>\n<p>The PSVR2 was confirmed by Sony to have 4K HDR imagery, 2000&#215;2040 per eye, and the field of view will also be wider than the original hardware at 110 degrees. <a href=\"https:\/\/blog.playstation.com\/2022\/01\/04\/playstation-vr2-and-playstation-vr2-sense-controller-the-next-generation-of-vr-gaming-on-ps5\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A blog post that appeared after the live announcement<\/a> confirmed rumors that it uses OLED and will have a 90-120 Hz refresh rate. (This paragraph has been updated with details from that post.)<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2253507\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It will however feature eye-tracking and foveated rendering, must-haves these days. Eye-tracking for obvious gameplay and other reasons, and foveated rendering so that the notoriously resource-hungry VR rendering process can focus its cycles on the area where the player is looking.<\/p>\n<p>One last and rather unexpected feature is force feedback in the headset. Whether people really want their heads vibrated is an open question, but you never know unless you try. A lot of people thought the Wii was a stupid idea.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2253517\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2253517\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2253517\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"583\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg 2129w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=150,85 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=300,171 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=768,437 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=680,387 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=1536,874 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=2048,1166 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/01\/psvr2-controllers.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2253517\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Sony<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>A new set of controllers will also come with the set, which will include their own improvements over the PSVR&#8217;s original two, which though perfectly fine at the time have been superseded by the competition&#8217;s capabilities. Sony actually <a href=\"https:\/\/blog.playstation.com\/2021\/03\/18\/next-gen-vr-on-ps5-the-new-controller\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">spilled the beans on these<\/a> a while back.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The company announced that a VR-only game in the Horizon series (started by Zero Dawn and to be continued soon with Forbidden West) will be among the many Sony first-party studios exclusives for the platform.<\/p>\n<p>More information is surely forthcoming, though this seems to be all we can expect from today&#8217;s event. We&#8217;ll update if we hear more.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/ces-2022\/?utm_source=internal&amp;utm_medium=footer-banner\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/12\/ces-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about CES 2022 on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Sony has announced some basic information about its much-anticipated next-generation VR hardware for the PS5, which it calls \u2014 predictably \u2014 PSVR2. Little was revealed about the device beyond its basic specs but it did confirm some features gamers will care about.
